## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear second-order oscillators. Common models combine restoring forces (often odd in x), damping forces (often odd in v), and optional external/parametric forcing functions of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (small oscillations, conservative linear spring)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper near equilibrium)
- Constant bias / gravity offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant load)
- Coulomb (dry) friction term: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (sliding friction dominated damping)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag / nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear stiffness (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (Duffing-type oscillator backbone curve)
- Piecewise-linear stiffness approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) (cubic-like hardening using |x|)
- Nonlinear damping (velocity-dependent coefficient): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * (c2 + x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent damping via x)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited oscillation): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (self-excited via v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (energy injection at small |v|)
- Simple pendulum form: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (nonlinear geometric restoring torque)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven vibration / resonance)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-like form)
- General potential-force form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (restoring force from polynomial potential + damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically appear as odd functions of x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)), reflecting symmetry and a stable equilibrium at x = 0.
- Damping forces typically oppose motion, appearing as terms odd in v (e.g., v, v*Abs(v), sign(v)); their net effect is to decrease mechanical energy over time.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles often arise when the effective damping changes sign with amplitude, captured by factors like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is indicated by the sign of the cubic term in x (positive x**3 term stiffens with amplitude; negative softens).
- External driving is usually periodic in t (sin/cos), enabling resonance and frequency-response effects that cannot be represented by x,v-only terms.
- Parametric excitation is suggested by time-modulation multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x), producing instability tongues and subharmonic responses.
- Geometric nonlinearities often replace linear x with sin(c*x) (pendulum-like), yielding amplitude-dependent frequency and non-sinusoidal motion.
- If acceleration depends strongly on both x and v via products (e.g., x*v, x**2*v), it often indicates state-dependent damping or nonlinear coupling from reduced-order models.
- Nonsmooth terms (Abs, sign) indicate impacts, dry friction, backlash, or other piecewise contact phenomena common in real oscillators.
